<a id="24923" class="Comment">-- Similar to the poset case, this is sufficient to establish that the category of frames</a>
<a id="25013" class="Comment">-- is univalent</a>

<a id="‚âÉf‚âÉ‚â°"></a><a id="25030" href="Frame.html#25030" class="Function">‚âÉf‚âÉ‚â°</a> <a id="25035" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="25037" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="25038" href="Frame.html#25038" class="Bound">F</a> <a id="25040" href="Frame.html#25040" class="Bound">G</a> <a id="25042" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="25044" href="Frame.html#3701" class="Function">Frame</a> <a id="25050" href="Basis.html#2320" class="Generalizable">‚Ñì‚ÇÄ</a> <a id="25053" href="Basis.html#2323" class="Generalizable">‚Ñì‚ÇÅ</a> <a id="25056" href="Basis.html#2326" class="Generalizable">‚Ñì‚ÇÇ</a><a id="25058" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="25060" class="Symbol">‚Üí</a> <a id="25062" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="25063" href="Frame.html#25038" class="Bound">F</a> <a id="25065" href="Frame.html#22508" class="Function Operator">‚âÉf</a> <a id="25068" href="Frame.html#25040" class="Bound">G</a><a id="25069" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="25071" href="Agda.Builtin.Cubical.Glue.html#1051" class="Function Operator">‚âÉ</a> <a id="25073" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="25074" href="Frame.html#25038" class="Bound">F</a> <a id="25076" href="Agda.Builtin.Cubical.Path.html#381" class="Function Operator">‚â°</a> <a id="25078" href="Frame.html#25040" class="Bound">G</a><a id="25079" class="Symbol">)</a>
<a id="25081" href="Frame.html#25030" class="Function">‚âÉf‚âÉ‚â°</a> <a id="25086" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="25088" href="Cubical.Foundations.SIP.html#4416" class="Function">SIP</a> <a id="25092" href="Frame.html#24797" class="Function">frame-is-univ-str</a>

<a id="25111" class="Comment">-- However, there are two minor issues with this.</a>
<a id="25161" class="Comment">--</a>
<a id="25164" class="Comment">--   1. We do not have to talk about equivalences as we are talking about sets;</a>
<a id="25244" class="Comment">--      isomorphisms are well-behaved in our case as we are dealing with sets.</a>
<a id="25323" class="Comment">--</a>
<a id="25326" class="Comment">--  2. We do not have to require the frame data to be preserved. We can show that any</a>
<a id="25412" class="Comment">--     poset isomorphism preserves the frame operators.</a>
<a id="25468" class="Comment">--</a>
<a id="25471" class="Comment">-- We will therefore strengthen our result to work with the notion of poset isomorphism.</a>

<a id="25561" class="Comment">-- We start by showing the equivalence between ‚âÉf and ‚âÖ‚Çö.</a>

<a id="31062" class="Comment">-- Now that we have this result, we can move on to show that given two frames F and G,</a>
<a id="31149" class="Comment">-- (pos F) ‚âÖ‚Çö (pos G) is equivalent to F ‚â° G.</a>
